     <p>
      The
      <b>
       Audi A3
      </b>
      is a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Small_family_car" title="Small family car">
       Small Family
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Compact_car" title="Compact car">
       Compact car
      </a>
      produced since 1996. The first two generations of A3 were based on the
      <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group_A_platform" title="Volkswagen Group A platform">
       Volkswagen Group A platform
      </a>
      , which they share with several other models such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Audi_TT" title="Audi TT">
       Audi TT
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf" title="Volkswagen Golf">
       Volkswagen Golf
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Caddy" title="Volkswagen Caddy">
       Volkswagen Caddy
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Touran" title="Volkswagen Touran">
       Volkswagen Touran
      </a>
      , as well as
      <a href="/wiki/SEAT_Le%C3%B3n" title="SEAT León">
       SEAT León
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/SEAT_Toledo" title="SEAT Toledo">
       SEAT Toledo
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0koda_Octavia" title="Škoda Octavia">
       Škoda Octavia
      </a>
      . The third-generation A3 uses the
      <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group_MQB_platform" title="Volkswagen Group MQB platform">
       Volkswagen Group MQB platform
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
      The original A3 (or
      <i>
       Typ
      </i>
      8L) was introduced in the European market in 1996, marking Audi's return to the production of smaller cars following the demise of the
      <a href="/wiki/Audi_50" title="Audi 50">
       Audi 50
      </a>
      in 1978. This was the first
      <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">
       Volkswagen Group
      </a>
      model to use the "PQ34" or "A4"
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile_platform" title="Automobile platform">
       platform
      </a>
      , bearing a close resemblance to the contemporary
      <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf_Mk4" title="Volkswagen Golf Mk4">
       Volkswagen Golf Mk4
      </a>
      , which arrived a year later. Within three years, this platform was used for total of seven cars.
     </p>
     <p>
      The A3 was initially available only with a three-door
      <a href="/wiki/Hatchback" title="Hatchback">
       hatchback
      </a>
      body, to present a more sporty image than the Golf, in both
      <a href="/wiki/Front-wheel_drive" title="Front-wheel drive">
       front
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">
       four-wheel drive
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Inline-four_engine" title="Inline-four engine">
       inline four-cylinder
      </a>
      engines were
      <a href="/wiki/Transverse_engine" title="Transverse engine">
       transversely mounted
      </a>
      . After the A4, the Audi A3 was the second model in the Audi lineup to use five valves per cylinder.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
       United Kingdom
      </a>
      market first received the Audi A3 in November 1996.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1999, Audi expanded the range with the introduction of more powerful versions: a 1.8 turbo rated 180 PS (132 kW; 178 hp), and a 1.9
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turbocharged_Direct_Injection" title="Turbocharged Direct Injection">
       TDI
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">
       diesel engine
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Unit_injector" title="Unit injector">
       unit injector
      </a>
      "Pumpe Düse" (PD) technology and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Variable_geometry_turbocharger" title="Variable geometry turbocharger">
       variable geometry turbocharger
      </a>
      . The four-wheel-drive A3 1.8T
      <a href="/wiki/Quattro_(four-wheel-drive_system)" title="Quattro (four-wheel-drive system)">
       quattro
      </a>
      used either the 150 PS (110 kW; 148 hp) or 180 PS (130 kW; 180 hp) engine, and the same
      <a href="/wiki/Haldex_Traction" title="Haldex Traction">
       Haldex Traction
      </a>
      -based four-wheel-drive system as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audi_S3" title="Audi S3">
       Audi S3
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Audi_TT" title="Audi TT">
       Audi TT
      </a>
      . Also in 1999, Audi also introduced a five-door body.
     </p>
     <p>
      In late 2000, the A3 range was revised with new headlights and rear lamps, other minor cosmetic changes, an improved interior, and the introduction of a six-speed
      <a href="/wiki/Manual_transmission" title="Manual transmission">
       manual
      </a>
      gearbox, on the 180 PS (132 kW; 178 hp) 1.8 Turbo and the new 130 PS (96 kW; 128 hp) 1.9 TDI.
     </p>
     <p>
      Audi's
      <a href="/wiki/Electronic_stability_control" title="Electronic stability control">
       electronic stability control
      </a>
      , traction-control, and brake force distribution computer became standard equipment in some countries.
     </p>
     <p>
      Although the first-generation Audi A3 was replaced in Europe in 2003, the first generation model continued to be sold in some markets. Production of the first generation model stopped in Brazil in 2006.
     </p>

     <p>
      Euro NCAP rating of 4 out of 5 stars.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EuroNCAPtest1_3-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-EuroNCAPtest1-3">
        [3]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Their evaluation concluded "the column lock, adjuster lever and bracket presented hazards in the knee impact area for the driver. These could cause high loads on his upper legs and damage to his knees." The A3 also provides almost no protection to pedestrians, giving it two stars out of a possible four.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EuroNCAPtest1_3-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-EuroNCAPtest1-3">
        [3]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div style="clear:both;">
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="S3_.281999.E2.80.932003.29">
       S3 (1999–2003)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: S3 (1999–2003)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2000_Audi_S3_(8L)_quattro_3-door_hatchback_(2015-05-29)_01.jpg">

       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">

       </div>

     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_S3_2002_Imola_Yellow_-_Flickr_-_The_Car_Spy_(1).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Audi_S3_2002_Imola_Yellow_-_Flickr_-_The_Car_Spy_%281%29.jpg/220px-Audi_S3_2002_Imola_Yellow_-_Flickr_-_The_Car_Spy_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Audi_S3_2002_Imola_Yellow_-_Flickr_-_The_Car_Spy_%281%29.jpg/330px-Audi_S3_2002_Imola_Yellow_-_Flickr_-_The_Car_Spy_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Audi_S3_2002_Imola_Yellow_-_Flickr_-_The_Car_Spy_%281%29.jpg/440px-Audi_S3_2002_Imola_Yellow_-_Flickr_-_The_Car_Spy_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_S3_2002_Imola_Yellow_-_Flickr_-_The_Car_Spy_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Audi S3 (facelift)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Audi released the A3-derived Audi S3 in 1999, only as a three-door hatchback. The inline-four
      <a href="/wiki/Multi-valve" title="Multi-valve">
       20v
      </a>
      1.8 L
      <a href="/wiki/Turbocharger" title="Turbocharger">
       turbocharged
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Petrol_engine" title="Petrol engine">
       petrol engine
      </a>
      come in two versions: 210 PS (154 kW; 207 hp) and 225 PS (165 kW; 222 hp). Early models (1999–2001) had 210 PS (154 kW; 207 hp). Later models (2001–2003) had
      <a href="/wiki/Variable_valve_timing" title="Variable valve timing">
       variable valve timing
      </a>
      and 225 PS (165 kW; 222 hp). The engine had a maximum of 280 N·m (210 ft·lbf)
      <a href="/wiki/Torque" title="Torque">
       torque
      </a>
      . This is the first time a small four-cylinder engine has been used in an
      <a href="/wiki/Audi_S_and_RS_models#S_models" title="Audi S and RS models">
       Audi S-series
      </a>
      car.
     </p>
     <p>
      Although dubbed
      <a href="/wiki/Quattro_(four-wheel-drive_system)" title="Quattro (four-wheel-drive system)">
       "quattro"
      </a>
      , the S3 uses a different
      <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">
       four-wheel drive
      </a>
      system.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autoportal_4-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autoportal-4">
        [4]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Haldex_Traction" title="Haldex Traction">
       Haldex Traction
      </a>
      coupling adjusts the bias of torque distribution from the front to rear axle as grip requirements change – most of the time it operates as a front-wheel drive.
     </p>
     <p>
      The S3 was sold in the Europe, Japan, Mexico, South Africa, Australia, and New Zealand.
     </p>
     <p>
      The S3 was facelifted in 2000, where it was given one-piece
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Headlights" title="Headlights">
       headlights
      </a>
      /indicator units, different front wings, rear lights clusters, and some minor upgrades to interior trim.
     </p>
     <p>
      Standard features include
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xenon_HID_headlamp" title="Xenon HID headlamp">
       xenon HID headlamps
      </a>
      with high pressure washers and auto levelers, front fog lamps, 17" "Avus"
      <a href="/wiki/Alloy_wheel" title="Alloy wheel">
       alloy wheels
      </a>
      with 225/45R17 tyres, electrically adjustable
      <a href="/wiki/Recaro" title="Recaro">
       Recaro
      </a>
      leather seats, climate control, alarm and electronic stability control with
      <a href="/wiki/Traction_control_system" title="Traction control system">
       traction control
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Options include a
      <a href="/wiki/Bose_Corporation" title="Bose Corporation">
       Bose
      </a>
      sound system, boot/trunk or in-dash mounted 6-disc
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CD_changer" title="CD changer">
       CD changer
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Metallic_paint" title="Metallic paint">
       metallic paint
      </a>
      , 18-inch 9-spoke RSTT wheels, glass
      <a href="/wiki/Sunroof" title="Sunroof">
       sunroof
      </a>
      , centre arm rest, privacy glass (B-pillar backwards), auto-dipping rear-view mirror, parking assist, luggage net, heated front seats,
      <a href="/wiki/Cruise_control" title="Cruise control">
       cruise control
      </a>
      , aluminium door mirror casings and part leather/
      <a href="/wiki/Alcantara_(material)" title="Alcantara (material)">
       alcantara
      </a>
      (blue/silver/yellow) combination seat coverings. These items are standard in some export markets.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Engines">
       Engines
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">

      </span>

      The engines used are the same as those for many other cars in the

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_release">
       Initial release
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Initial release">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      At the 2003
      <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Motor_Show" title="Geneva Motor Show">
       Geneva Motor Show
      </a>
      , Audi launched the second generation of the A3, the
      <i>
       Typ
      </i>
      8P, designed by Gary Telaak during 2000 (however, the final design was frozen in 2001). Originally launched only as a three-door
      <a href="/wiki/Hatchback" title="Hatchback">
       hatchback
      </a>
      with four-cylinder engines, it featured a new
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile_platform" title="Automobile platform">
       automobile platform
      </a>
      (the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volkswagen_A_platform#PQ35" title="Volkswagen A platform">
       PQ35
      </a>
      platform), a redesigned and more spacious interior, new
      <a href="/wiki/Petrol_engine" title="Petrol engine">
       petrol engines
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Gasoline_direct_injection" title="Gasoline direct injection">
       Fuel Stratified Injection
      </a>
      (FSI), and standard six-speed manual gearboxes (except on the base 1.6).
     </p>
     <p>
      In mid-2003, the line was updated with two sports-oriented models, a 2.0 Turbo-FSI version rated 200 PS (147 kW; 197 hp), and a 3.2 L
      <a href="/wiki/VR6_engine" title="VR6 engine">
       VR6 engine
      </a>
      (for the first time) with 250 PS (184 kW; 247 hp).
      <a href="/wiki/Haldex_Traction" title="Haldex Traction">
       Haldex Traction
      </a>
      -based
      <a href="/wiki/Quattro_(four-wheel-drive_system)" title="Quattro (four-wheel-drive system)">
       quattro
      </a>
      on-demand four-wheel drive, and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct-Shift_Gearbox" title="Direct-Shift Gearbox">
       S-Tronic
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Semi-automatic_transmission" title="Semi-automatic transmission">
       semi-auto gearbox
      </a>
      were introduced as options (quattro is standard on the VR6) on models with engines over 140 PS (103 kW; 138 hp).
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2005, the "S line" trim level, offering new decorative elements, became available and the three-door A3 received the same front end styling features as the Sportback model. For the first time, the A3 became available in the
      <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">
       North American
      </a>
      market, exclusively with the Sportback body, with the base 2.0
      <a href="/wiki/Inline-four_engine" title="Inline-four engine">
       inline-four
      </a>
      TFSI introduced in 2005 as a 2006 model, and the 3.2 VR6 quattro following.
     </p>
     <table class="wikitable">
      <tr>
       <th>
        Chassis codes
       </th>

       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="A3_Sportback_.282004.E2.80.93.29">
       A3 Sportback (2004–)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: A3 Sportback (2004–)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The five-door "Sportback" model was introduced in June 2004. The A3 Sportback is 80 mm (3 in) longer than the base three-door body, and includes improved rear cabin space and a larger luggage compartment (370 litres). It also received the new "single frame" front grille originally introduced in the
      <a href="/wiki/Audi_A8" title="Audi A8">
       A8 W12
      </a>
      , which was later adopted across the whole A3 range.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="S3_.282006.E2.80.932012.29">
       S3 (2006–2012)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: S3 (2006–2012)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_S3_Sprintblau.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1069" data-file-width="1500" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Audi_S3_Sprintblau.JPG/220px-Audi_S3_Sprintblau.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Audi_S3_Sprintblau.JPG/330px-Audi_S3_Sprintblau.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Audi_S3_Sprintblau.JPG/440px-Audi_S3_Sprintblau.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_S3_Sprintblau.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Audi S3 3 door hatchback
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_s3_back_white.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1526" data-file-width="2527" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Audi_s3_back_white.jpg/220px-Audi_s3_back_white.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Audi_s3_back_white.jpg/330px-Audi_s3_back_white.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Audi_s3_back_white.jpg/440px-Audi_s3_back_white.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_s3_back_white.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Audi S3 3-door hatchback
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In August 2006, Audi announced the second generation S3. Offered in three- and five-door body styles, the second generation—
      <i>
       Typ
      </i>
      8P—S3 is powered by a modified and uprated
      <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">
       Volkswagen Group
      </a>
      -sourced 2.0-litre turbocharged
      <a href="/wiki/Gasoline_direct_injection" title="Gasoline direct injection">
       FSI
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Petrol_engine" title="Petrol engine">
       petrol engine
      </a>
      , with a maximum output of 195
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilowatt" title="Kilowatt">
       kW
      </a>
      (265
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metric_horsepower" title="Metric horsepower">
       PS
      </a>
      ; 261
      <a href="/wiki/Horsepower#Brake_horsepower" title="Horsepower">
       bhp
      </a>
      ). As with all
      <a href="/wiki/Audi_S_and_RS_models" title="Audi S and RS models">
       Audi S models
      </a>
      , the design was done in-house by
      <a href="/wiki/Quattro_GmbH" title="Quattro GmbH">
       quattro GmbH
      </a>
      . The engine features uprated high-performance
      <a href="/wiki/Piston" title="Piston">
       pistons
      </a>
      , revised boost/fuel mapping, increased turbocharger size (KKK K04) and larger
      <a href="/wiki/Intercooler" title="Intercooler">
       intercooler
      </a>
      . The most powerful form of this engine, and
      <a href="/wiki/Quattro_(four-wheel-drive_system)" title="Quattro (four-wheel-drive system)">
       quattro
      </a>
      four-wheel drive, makes for a 0–100 km/h (0–62 mph) time of 5.5 s, and an electronically limited top speed of 250 km/h (155 mph). Audi offers both six-speed manual and six-speed
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct-Shift_Gearbox" title="Direct-Shift Gearbox">
       S-Tronic
      </a>
      automatic transmissions with the S3.
     </p>
     <p>
      The spring ratings and dampers were revised, along with the body kit. Like its predecessor, although badged a "quattro" model, the S3 does not employ a
      <a href="/wiki/Torsen" title="Torsen">
       Torsen
      </a>
      centre differential (as in other common quattro models), but instead uses the Swedish
      <a href="/wiki/Haldex_Traction" title="Haldex Traction">
       Haldex Traction
      </a>
      system in its on-demand
      <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">
       four-wheel drive
      </a>
      transmission, due to the
      <a href="/wiki/Transverse_engine" title="Transverse engine">
       transverse engine
      </a>
      layout.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Safety_2">

       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>

          <img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          <img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/11px-Star_empty.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/17px-Star_empty.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/22px-Star_empty.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          <img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/11px-Star_empty.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/17px-Star_empty.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/22px-Star_empty.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Pedestrian:
        </td>
        <td style="text-align:center;">
         8
        </td>
        <td style="text-align:center;">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap" title="1 /4 stars">
          <img alt="1 /4 stars" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" title="1 /4 stars" width="11"/>
          <img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/11px-Star_empty.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/17px-Star_empty.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/22px-Star_empty.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          <img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/11px-Star_empty.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/17px-Star_empty.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/22px-Star_empty.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          <img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/11px-Star_empty.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/17px-Star_empty.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/22px-Star_empty.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
     </div>
     <p>
      Euro NCAP tested a second generation Audi A3 with front airbags, side airbags, seatbelt pretensioners and load limiters as standard. Despite Audi increasing the protection inside the car for the driver and passengers, pedestrian safety actually got 33% worse compared to the first generation and Euro NCAP gave criticism for the car offering virtually no protection at all on the front end and scoring just one star from a possible four. "A poor result for a new car" was the verdict given for pedestrian safety after the test.
     </p>
     <div style="clear:both;">
     </div>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2008_update">
       2008 update
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2008 update">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Audi introduced a number of changes to the A3 and S3 in 2008. These include revised nose and tail styling, with a modified grille and the new "trademark" daytime running lights,
      <a href="/wiki/Common_rail" title="Common rail">
       common rail
      </a>
      2.0 TDI engines, seven-speed S tronic
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dual_clutch_transmission" title="Dual clutch transmission">
       dual clutch transmission
      </a>
      availability for the smaller non-U.S. engines, and optional "magnetic ride" adaptive
      <a href="/wiki/Shock_absorber" title="Shock absorber">
       shock absorbers
      </a>
      . In addition, the range now includes an S3 Sportback model.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        [9]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Also, a cabriolet version was introduced. It was similar dimensions to the 3-door version, with a two-box design.
     </p>

             <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_A3_Sportback_TDI_Ambition_(8PA,_3._Facelift)_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht,_3._M%C3%A4rz_2012,_Ratingen.jpg" title="2010–2012 Audi A3 Sportback">

     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Audi_A3_TDI_Clubsport_quattro_.282008.29">
       Audi A3 TDI Clubsport quattro (2008)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Audi A3 TDI Clubsport quattro (2008)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      <b>
       Audi A3 TDI Clubsport quattro
      </b>
      is a
      <a href="/wiki/Concept_car" title="Concept car">
       concept car
      </a>
      unveiled in 2008. Based on the Audi A3 three-door, it is an approach by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audi_AG" title="Audi AG">
       Audi
      </a>
      to address both performance and the environment.
     </p>
     <p>
      The engine in the concept car is a turbocharged 2.0-litre diesel producing 224 horsepower (167 kW) and 332 lb·ft (450 N·m). of torque. It produces 113.8 horsepower (84.9 kW) per litre while meeting Euro 5 Diesel emission standards. It uses the
      <a href="/wiki/Quattro_(four-wheel-drive_system)" title="Quattro (four-wheel-drive system)">
       quattro
      </a>
      drive system with a six-speed manual transmission.
     </p>
     <p>
      The chassis has Audi's Magnetic Ride Suspension system, lowering the vehicle 1.4 inches (36 mm) from the base model. It also has ceramic front brakes, a four-link rear suspension and electro-mechanical servo assist for the
      <a href="/wiki/Rack_and_pinion" title="Rack and pinion">
       rack and pinion
      </a>
      steering.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qq_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-qq-10">
        [10]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Exterior modifications include the widening of the three-door's grill, modifying the odd, and enlarging air intakes. Bolt-on fender flares and a large rear spoiler have been added. The interior changes include sport seats and a flat-bottomed steering wheel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qq_10-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-qq-10">
        [10]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Audi claims performance of 0 to 62 mph (0 to 100 km/h) in 6.6 seconds with a top speed of 149 mph (240 km/h).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        [11]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is expected to get approximately 40 miles per US gallon (5.9 L/100 km; 48 mpg
      <sub>
       <small>
        -imp
       </small>
      </sub>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        [12]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="RS_3_Sportback_.282011.E2.80.932012.29">
       <span id="RS3">
       </span>
       <span id="RS_3">
       </span>
       RS 3 Sportback (2011–2012)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: RS 3 Sportback (2011–2012)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_RS3_Sportback_Daytonagrau.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1676" data-file-width="2514" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Audi_RS3_Sportback_Daytonagrau.JPG/220px-Audi_RS3_Sportback_Daytonagrau.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Audi_RS3_Sportback_Daytonagrau.JPG/330px-Audi_RS3_Sportback_Daytonagrau.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Audi_RS3_Sportback_Daytonagrau.JPG/440px-Audi_RS3_Sportback_Daytonagrau.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_RS3_Sportback_Daytonagrau.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Audi RS 3 Sportback
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_RS3_Sportback_(10961583406).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3216" data-file-width="4140" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Audi_RS3_Sportback_%2810961583406%29.jpg/220px-Audi_RS3_Sportback_%2810961583406%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Audi_RS3_Sportback_%2810961583406%29.jpg/330px-Audi_RS3_Sportback_%2810961583406%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Audi_RS3_Sportback_%2810961583406%29.jpg/440px-Audi_RS3_Sportback_%2810961583406%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_RS3_Sportback_(10961583406).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Audi RS 3 sportback
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Audi RS 3 is derivative of the A3 Sportback with a
      <a href="/wiki/Straight-five_engine" title="Straight-five engine">
       5-cylinder
      </a>
      , 2,480 cc (151 cu in) turbocharged engine rated 340 PS (250 kW; 335 hp) and 450 N·m (332 lb·ft), vermicular-graphite cast iron crankcase, seven-speed
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct-Shift_Gearbox" title="Direct-Shift Gearbox">
       S tronic
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Transmission_(mechanics)" title="Transmission (mechanics)">
       transmission
      </a>
      with two automatic modes and one manual mode,
      <a href="/wiki/Quattro_(four-wheel-drive_system)" title="Quattro (four-wheel-drive system)">
       Quattro
      </a>
      on-demand
      <a href="/wiki/Four-wheel_drive" title="Four-wheel drive">
       four-wheel drive
      </a>
      system, widened track to 1,564 mm (61.57 in),
      <a href="/wiki/MacPherson_strut" title="MacPherson strut">
       MacPherson strut
      </a>
      in aluminum, lowered body by 25 mm (0.98 in), 19-inch cast aluminum wheels in machine-polished titanium styling (optional black with a red rim flange) with 235/35 front and 225/35 rear tires, 370 mm (14.57 in) front and 310 mm (12.20 in) ventilated brake discs, aluminum brake disk covers, four-piston fixed calipers in high-gloss black with RS logos, electronic stabilization program with Sport mode, flared front fenders made of carbon-fiber-reinforced plastic (CFRP), prominent sill panels and exterior-mirror casings in matte aluminum, roof spoiler, high-gloss black diffusor insert, two elliptical exhaust tailpipes on the left, black interior, sports seats upholstered in Fine Nappa leather with silver contrasting stitching, inlays in Piano black finish or Aluminum Race colour, flat-bottomed leather multifunction sports steering wheel, choice of 5 body colors are available with an unlimited selection of custom paint finishes. It's
      <a href="/wiki/Acceleration" title="Acceleration">
       acceleration
      </a>
      is quoted as 0 to 62 mph (0 to 100 km/h) in 4.6
      <a href="/wiki/Second" title="Second">
       seconds
      </a>
      , with an electronically limited top speed of 155 mph (249 km/h). Optional features included front bucket seats, roof rails in matte aluminum look, styling packages in black or matte aluminum.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        [13]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      First deliveries started in early 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-audi-rs3_14-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-audi-rs3-14">
        [14]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="A3_Cabriolet_Sport_and_S_line_Final_Edition_.282013.E2.80.93.29">
       A3 Cabriolet Sport and S line Final Edition (2013–)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: A3 Cabriolet Sport and S line Final Edition (2013–)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      A3 Cabriolet Sport Final Edition is a version of A3 Cabriolet Sport model for the UK market, commemorating the end of A3 Cabriolet's production run. It included Vienna leather upholstery, front seat heating, rear parking sensors, automatic headlight and wiper activation, cruise control, a Bluetooth mobile phone interface.
     </p>
     <p>
      S line Final Edition is based on the A3 Cabriolet Sport Final Edition model, with 18-inch S line alloy wheel with a new five-segment spoke design, full Vienna leather upholstery, S line safety and entertainment features with xenon plus headlights with LED daytime running lamps, DVD-based satellite-navigation, Audi Music Interface iPod connection, a BOSE sound system.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        [15]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Production">
       Production
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Production">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Engines_2">
       Engines
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Engines">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In January 2007, the normally aspirated (non-turbo) 2.0 FSI was replaced by a new turbocharged 1.8 TFSI engine rated 160 PS (118 kW; 158 hp). It is available in front-wheel drive only.
     </p>
     <p>
      In late 2007, Audi introduced a new 125 PS (92 kW; 123 hp) 1.4 L TFSI engine for the A3, replacing the 1.6 L FSI engine, and a new diesel "e"-model. The "e"-model, Audi's equivalent of Volkswagen's
      <a href="/wiki/BlueMotion" title="BlueMotion">
       BlueMotion
      </a>
      , is available with the 1.9 L TDI engine, and offers a more ecological car, with a
      <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">
       CO
       <sub>
        2
       </sub>
      </a>
      emission below 120 g/km.
     </p>
     <p>
      In June 2009, Audi announced the release of two models of A3 1.6
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turbocharged_Direct_Injection" title="Turbocharged Direct Injection">
       TDI
      </a>
      for European market. The first uses Audi's start/stop and energy recovery system, and will produce 105 PS (77 kW; 104 hp). This engine will achieve approximately 4.1 L/100 km (69 mpg
      <sub>
       <small>
        -imp
       </small>
      </sub>
      ; 57 mpg
      <sub>
       <small>
        -US
       </small>
      </sub>
      ).
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
         <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (October 2009)">
          clarification needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      The second engine does not use the same efficiency systems and will produce 90 PS (66 kW; 89 hp) will get 4.5 L/100 km (63 mpg
      <sub>
       <small>
        -imp
       </small>
      </sub>
      ; 52 mpg
      <sub>
       <small>
        -US
       </small>
      </sub>
      ). They went on sale in June 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        [16]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In August 2009, Audi announced that the 1.6 L eight-valve petrol engine would be replaced by a turbocharged 1.2 TFSI engine already found in VW's Polo and Golf models. This engine is rated at 105 PS (77 kW; 104 hp) and 175 N·m (129 lb·ft), emitting 127 g/km of CO
      <sub>
       2
      </sub>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-audi-1.2tfsi_17-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-audi-1.2tfsi-17">
        [17]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of April 2010, Audi has yet to release official specifications or prices for the 1.2 TSI model, as the 1.6 model has been made a special clearance model for clearing out 1.6 stock.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The A3 2.0 TDI clean diesel is a version of Audi's A3 2.0 TDI for the North American market, making it the second Audi TDI vehicle sold in North America, following the
      <a href="/wiki/Audi_Q7" title="Audi Q7">
       Audi Q7
      </a>
      TDI in 2008. It is a FWD vehicle with S-tronic transmission with Hill-hold assist, Sirius satellite radio, Leather seats and steering wheel, Auxiliary audio input, Dual-zone climate control, 17 in (432 mm) alloy wheels. The vehicle was unveiled at the
      <a href="/wiki/North_American_International_Auto_Show#2009" title="North American International Auto Show">
       2009 North American International Auto Show
      </a>
      . This US model would begin sale in the first quarter of 2010 as a 2010 model year vehicle.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        [18]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In March 2011, the line-up was expanded with the introduction of a more powerful 2.0
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turbocharged_Direct_Injection" title="Turbocharged Direct Injection">
       TDI
      </a>
      with 170 PS (125 kW; 168 hp).
     </p>
     <p>
      The 2012 Audi 2.0L I4 TDI produces 140 hp (104 kW) and 236 lb·ft (320 N·m) of torque
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      and will go from 0 to 60 mph (0 to 97 km/h) in 8.9 seconds.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        [19]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The 2.0 TDI engine was included in the engines found by the United States Environmental Protection Agency to use software intentionally designed to turn off emission control systems except when undergoing emission testing.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        [20]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Models made from 2009 to 2015 were affected.
     </p>

        4-door: 4,456 mm (175.4 in)
        <br/>
        5-door: 4,310 mm (169.7 in)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A3_dim_26-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-A3_dim-26">
          [26]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th scope="row">
        Width
       </th>
       <td>
        3-door: 1,777 mm (70.0 in)
        <br/>
        4-door: 1,796 mm (70.7 in)
        <br/>
        5-door: 1,785 mm (70.3 in)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A3_dim_26-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-A3_dim-26">

         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th scope="row">
        Height
       </th>
       <td>
        3-door: 1,421 mm (55.9 in)
        <br/>
        4-door: 1,416 mm (55.7 in)
        <br/>
        5-door: 1,421 mm (55.9 in)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A3_dim_26-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-A3_dim-26">
          [26]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th scope="row">
        <a href="/wiki/Curb_weight" title="Curb weight">
         Kerb weight
        </a>
       </th>
       <td>
        1,150 kg (2,535 lb) to
        <br/>
        1,520 kg (3,351 lb)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
         <a href="#cite_note-27">
          [27]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015_Audi_RS3_Sportback_revealed_28-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-2015_Audi_RS3_Sportback_revealed-28">
          [28]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2014_Audi_A3_(8V_MY15)_1.8_TFSI_Ambition_convertible_(2015-07-24)_02.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2856" data-file-width="4272" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/2014_Audi_A3_%288V_MY15%29_1.8_TFSI_Ambition_convertible_%282015-07-24%29_02.jpg/220px-2014_Audi_A3_%288V_MY15%29_1.8_TFSI_Ambition_convertible_%282015-07-24%29_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/2014_Audi_A3_%288V_MY15%29_1.8_TFSI_Ambition_convertible_%282015-07-24%29_02.jpg/330px-2014_Audi_A3_%288V_MY15%29_1.8_TFSI_Ambition_convertible_%282015-07-24%29_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/2014_Audi_A3_%288V_MY15%29_1.8_TFSI_Ambition_convertible_%282015-07-24%29_02.jpg/440px-2014_Audi_A3_%288V_MY15%29_1.8_TFSI_Ambition_convertible_%282015-07-24%29_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2014_Audi_A3_(8V_MY15)_1.8_TFSI_Ambition_convertible_(2015-07-24)_02.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Audi A3 Cabriolet
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_A3_S_line_TFSI_Porschegr%C3%BCn_Heck.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1658" data-file-width="2761" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Audi_A3_S_line_TFSI_Porschegr%C3%BCn_Heck.jpg/220px-Audi_A3_S_line_TFSI_Porschegr%C3%BCn_Heck.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Audi_A3_S_line_TFSI_Porschegr%C3%BCn_Heck.jpg/330px-Audi_A3_S_line_TFSI_Porschegr%C3%BCn_Heck.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Audi_A3_S_line_TFSI_Porschegr%C3%BCn_Heck.jpg/440px-Audi_A3_S_line_TFSI_Porschegr%C3%BCn_Heck.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_A3_S_line_TFSI_Porschegr%C3%BCn_Heck.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Audi A3 3-door Sportback
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The vehicle was unveiled in 2012 Geneva Motor Show.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        [29]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        [30]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and went on sale in Europe in September 2012.
     </p>
     <p>
      First vehicle using the flexible modular
      <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group_MQB_platform" title="Volkswagen Group MQB platform">
       Volkswagen Group MQB platform
      </a>
      , the third generation is available as a three-door hatchback, a five-door "Sportback", a four-door
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saloon_(automobile)" title="Saloon (automobile)">
       saloon
      </a>
      to directly rival the
      <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_CLA-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz CLA-Class">
       Mercedes-Benz CLA-Class
      </a>
      , and a two-door Cabriolet.
     </p>
     <p>
      The front suspension is a
      <a href="/wiki/MacPherson_strut" title="MacPherson strut">
       MacPherson strut
      </a>
      set-up while the rear utilizes multi-link rear suspension.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autocar-2012_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autocar-2012-31">
        [31]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The features include:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multi-collision_brake" title="Multi-collision brake">
        Multi-collision brake
       </a>
       : Emergency braking function stops the car after the first impact, to prevent secondary collisions
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Multi_Media_Interface" title="Multi Media Interface">
        Multi Media Interface
       </a>
       MMI entertainment system (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tegra_3" title="Tegra 3">
        Tegra 3
       </a>
       processor) with
       <a href="/wiki/Handwriting_recognition" title="Handwriting recognition">
        handwriting recognition
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/4G" title="4G">
        4G
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadband_internet" title="Broadband internet">
        broadband internet
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adaptive_cruise_control" title="Adaptive cruise control">
        adaptive cruise control
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre_sense" title="Pre sense">
        Pre sense
       </a>
       front/basic
       <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">
        radar
       </a>
       -guided
       <a href="/wiki/Collision_avoidance_system" title="Collision avoidance system">
        collision avoidance system
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Active_lane_assist" title="Active lane assist">
        active lane assist
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Side_assist" title="Side assist">
        side assist
       </a>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      Early German models include 1.4 TFSI (122 PS), 1.8 TFSI (180 PS), and 2.0 TDI (150 PS).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-audi-mediaservices.com_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-audi-mediaservices.com-33">
        [33]
       </a>
      </sup>
      1.2 TFSI (105 PS), 1.4 TFSI (140 PS), 1.8 TFSI quattro (180 PS), 1.6 TDI (105 PS), and 2.0 TDI quattro (150 PS) were added in 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_34-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-34">
        [34]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A3 1.2 TFSI (105 PS) was added to the UK market in 2013,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        [35]
       </a>
      </sup>
      followed by A3 1.4 TFSI (140 PS) in 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-audi.co.uk_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-audi.co.uk-36">
        [36]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="A3_Sedan_.282013.E2.80.93.29">
       A3 Sedan (2013–)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: A3 Sedan (2013–)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_A3_Limousine_TFSI_Ambiente_(8V)_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht,_1._September_2013,_M%C3%BCnster.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1667" data-file-width="3375" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Audi_A3_Limousine_TFSI_Ambiente_%288V%29_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht%2C_1._September_2013%2C_M%C3%BCnster.jpg/220px-Audi_A3_Limousine_TFSI_Ambiente_%288V%29_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht%2C_1._September_2013%2C_M%C3%BCnster.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Audi_A3_Limousine_TFSI_Ambiente_%288V%29_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht%2C_1._September_2013%2C_M%C3%BCnster.jpg/330px-Audi_A3_Limousine_TFSI_Ambiente_%288V%29_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht%2C_1._September_2013%2C_M%C3%BCnster.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Audi_A3_Limousine_TFSI_Ambiente_%288V%29_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht%2C_1._September_2013%2C_M%C3%BCnster.jpg/440px-Audi_A3_Limousine_TFSI_Ambiente_%288V%29_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht%2C_1._September_2013%2C_M%C3%BCnster.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_A3_Limousine_TFSI_Ambiente_(8V)_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht,_1._September_2013,_M%C3%BCnster.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Audi A3 TFSI Ambiente (Europe)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The A3 Sedan includes a body 11 mm (0.43 in) wider and 9 mm (0.35 in) lower than that of the A3 Sportback. Other features include 16- to 18-inch-wheels (optional 19-inch wheels via quattro GmbH) and electronic stabilization control with electronic differential lock.
     </p>
     <p>
      The vehicle was unveiled at the 2013 New York Auto Show.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        [37]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The German model was set to go on sale in late summer 2013. Early models include 1.4 TFSI (140 PS), 1.8 TFSI (180 PS), and 2.0 TDI (150 PS).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_38-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-38">
        [38]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Delivery of the UK models began in autumn of 2013. Early models include 1.4 TFSI (140 PS), 1.8 TFSI (180 PS), and 2.0 TDI (150 PS).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_39-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-39">
        [39]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="A3_Cabrio_.282013.E2.80.93.29">
       A3 Cabrio (2013–)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: A3 Cabrio (2013–)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The A3 cabriolet model is available from 2014. It has a three-box bodystyle and a larger boot than the previous model (320 litres versus 260).
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="S3_.282013.E2.80.93.29">
       S3 (2013–)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: S3 (2013–)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_S3_Sportback_(8V)_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht,_6._M%C3%A4rz_2016,_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1711" data-file-width="3449" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Audi_S3_Sportback_%288V%29_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht%2C_6._M%C3%A4rz_2016%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/220px-Audi_S3_Sportback_%288V%29_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht%2C_6._M%C3%A4rz_2016%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Audi_S3_Sportback_%288V%29_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht%2C_6._M%C3%A4rz_2016%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/330px-Audi_S3_Sportback_%288V%29_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht%2C_6._M%C3%A4rz_2016%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Audi_S3_Sportback_%288V%29_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht%2C_6._M%C3%A4rz_2016%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg/440px-Audi_S3_Sportback_%288V%29_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht%2C_6._M%C3%A4rz_2016%2C_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Audi_S3_Sportback_(8V)_%E2%80%93_Heckansicht,_6._M%C3%A4rz_2016,_D%C3%BCsseldorf.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Audi S3 Sportback
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The third generation Audi S3 is powered by a 2.0-litre
      <a href="/wiki/Turbo_fuel_stratified_injection" title="Turbo fuel stratified injection">
       TFSI petrol engine
      </a>
      , with an output of 221
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilowatt" title="Kilowatt">
       kW
      </a>
      (300
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metric_horsepower" title="Metric horsepower">
       PS
      </a>
      ; 296
      <a href="/wiki/Horsepower#Brake_horsepower" title="Horsepower">
       bhp
      </a>
      ). It features new
      <a href="/wiki/Piston" title="Piston">
       pistons
      </a>
      with stronger bolts and new rings, as well as reinforced connecting rods with new mounts transferring the power to the
      <a href="/wiki/Crankshaft" title="Crankshaft">
       crankshaft
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Cylinder_head" title="Cylinder head">
       cylinder head
      </a>
      is made of a new lightweight aluminium alloy designed with high strength and temperature resistance in mind. The engine is capable of delivering 380 Nm from 1,800–5,500 rpm, with its limit being at 6,800 rpm. The 4 cylinder engine has a combined fuel economy of 23 mpg manual (24 mpg
      <i>
       S Tronic
      </i>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      The engine weighs in at 148 kilograms (326 lb), 5 kilograms (11 lb) lighter than the previous generation. The S3 is capable of 0–100 km/h (0–62 mph) in 4.9 seconds when equipped with a manual transmission, or 4.7 seconds when using the S tronic, and has an electronically limited top speed of 155 miles per hour (249 km/h).
     </p>
     <div style="clear:both;">
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="A3_Sportback_.282013.E2.80.93.29">
       A3 Sportback (2013–)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: A3 Sportback (2013–)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2015_Audi_A3_(8V_MY15)_Attraction_5-door_hatchback_(2015-06-08)_02.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2856" data-file-width="4272" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/2015_Audi_A3_%288V_MY15%29_Attraction_5-door_hatchback_%282015-06-08%29_02.jpg/220px-2015_Audi_A3_%288V_MY15%29_Attraction_5-door_hatchback_%282015-06-08%29_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/2015_Audi_A3_%288V_MY15%29_Attraction_5-door_hatchback_%282015-06-08%29_02.jpg/330px-2015_Audi_A3_%288V_MY15%29_Attraction_5-door_hatchback_%282015-06-08%29_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/2015_Audi_A3_%288V_MY15%29_Attraction_5-door_hatchback_%282015-06-08%29_02.jpg/440px-2015_Audi_A3_%288V_MY15%29_Attraction_5-door_hatchback_%282015-06-08%29_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2015_Audi_A3_(8V_MY15)_Attraction_5-door_hatchback_(2015-06-08)_02.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Audi A3 Sportback
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Audi A3 Sportback includes a wheelbase 58 mm (2.28 in) over previous model, 35 mm (1.38 in) longer than that of the A3 and a front axle shifted forward by 40 mm (1.57 in) over the previous model. Other features include a choice of 13 body colours (three solid finishes, eight metallic finishes and two pearl-effect finishes), optional high-gloss package adding accents around the windows (standard with the Ambiente trim line), six-speed manual transmission (optional S tronic) for all engine models, 16 or 17-inch wheels depending on trim line (optional 18-inch wheels), Audi drive select (standard with Ambition) with optional S tronic, and optional
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_damper" title="Electromagnetic damper">
       electromagnetic damper
      </a>
      control system.
     </p>
     <p>
      German models went on sale in February 2013. Early models include 1.4 TFSI (122 PS), 1.8 TFSI (180 PS), 1.8 TFSI quattro (180 PS), and 1.6 TDI. 1.2 TFSI (105 PS), 1.4 TFSI (140 PS), 2.0 TDI (150 PS), 2.0 TDI quattro (150 PS), and 2.0 TDI (184 PS) were available in later date.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="A3_Sportback_g-tron_.282013.E2.80.93.29">
       A3 Sportback g-tron (2013–)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: A3 Sportback g-tron (2013–)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_7921.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_7921.JPG/220px-2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_7921.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_7921.JPG/330px-2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_7921.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_7921.JPG/440px-2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_7921.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2013-03-05_Geneva_Motor_Show_7921.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Audi A3 Sportback g-tron
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      It is a version of the A3 Sportback with 1.4 TFSI (110 PS) engine powered by compressed natural gas or Audi e-gas synthetic methane; gas tank made of gas-impermeable polyamide polymer, carbon fiber-reinforced polymer, glass fiber reinforced polymer; and an electronic gas pressure regulator. The synthetic methane was produced by waste product from a nearby Werlte biogas plant operated by power utility EWE.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        [40]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A production model was to be available by the end of 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_34-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-34">
        [34]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div style="clear:both;">
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="A3_Sportback_e-tron_.282014.E2.80.93.29">
       A3 Sportback e-tron (2014–)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: A3 Sportback e-tron (2014–)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">
       plug-in hybrid
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Concept_car" title="Concept car">
       concept car
      </a>
      was unveiled at the 2013
      <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Motor_Show" title="Geneva Motor Show">
       Geneva Motor Show
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        [41]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In May 2013 Audi confirmed its decision to produce a plug-in hybrid version of the A3, the Audi A3 Sportback e-tron, which was scheduled for retail sales in Europe by late 2013, and by mid 2014 in the U.S. and the UK.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A3etron_42-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-A3etron-42">
        [42]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A3etron02_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-A3etron02-43">
        [43]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The A3 e-tron shares the same plug-in hybrid powertrain used in both the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf_GTE" title="Volkswagen Golf GTE">
       Volkswagen Golf GTE
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Passat_GTE" title="Volkswagen Passat GTE">
       Passat GTE
      </a>
      .To charge the A3 e-tron, the Audi four rings logo
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        [44]
       </a>
      </sup>
      is pulled along to reveal a charging socket.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        [45]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The A3 Sportback e-tron is powered by a 1.4 L TSI gasoline engine that delivers 148 bhp and 184 lb ft, coupled with a 101 bhp electric motor, which is integrated into the car's six-speed dual-clutch automatic transmission, for a total combined output of 201 bhp and 243 lb ft. The plug-in hybrid has an 8.8
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KWh" title="KWh">
       kWh
      </a>
      battery pack that delivers an
      <a href="/wiki/All-electric_range" title="All-electric range">
       all-electric range
      </a>
      of 50 km (31 mi) on the
      <a href="/wiki/New_European_Driving_Cycle" title="New European Driving Cycle">
       NEDC
      </a>
      cycle, and a total of 940 km (580 mi). The plug-in hybrid can reach a top speed of 220 km/h (140 mph) and can reach 100 km/h (62 mph) in 7.6 seconds. According to Audi the car has an average fuel efficiency of 188 mpg equivalent and CO2 emissions of 35 g/km.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A3etron_42-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-A3etron-42">
        [42]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A3etron02_43-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-A3etron02-43">
        [43]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In September 2013, at the Frankfurt Motor Show, Audi announced the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audi_A3_Sportback_e-tron" title="Audi A3 Sportback e-tron">
       Audi A3 Sportback e-tron
      </a>
      would be available in Europe in the second quarter of 2014 at a price of €37,000 Euros (
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       US$45,500
      </span>
      ,
      <span style="white-space: nowrap">
       GB£30,500
      </span>
      ),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        [46]
       </a>
      </sup>
      but it slipped to orders in the second quarter of 2014, with deliveries slated for the third quarter. On August 1, 2014, Audi announced the A3 Sportback e-Tron was on sale across Europe.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        [47]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The first 227 units were registered in Germany in August 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Germany082014_48-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Germany082014-48">
        [48]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of December 2015
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , global sales totaled 12,994 units, of which, 12,945 units were registered in Europe,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europe2015_49-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Europe2015-49">
        [49]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and 49 units in the United States, where deliveries began in December 2015.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        [50]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div style="clear:both;">
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="RS_3_Sportback_.282015.E2.80.932016.29">
       RS 3 Sportback (2015–2016)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: RS 3 Sportback (2015–2016)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AudiRs3_8V.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1766" data-file-width="2837" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/AudiRs3_8V.jpg/220px-AudiRs3_8V.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/AudiRs3_8V.jpg/330px-AudiRs3_8V.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/AudiRs3_8V.jpg/440px-AudiRs3_8V.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AudiRs3_8V.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Audi RS 3 sportback (8V)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Details for the RS 3 Sportback were revealed in December 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015_Audi_RS3_Sportback_revealed_28-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-2015_Audi_RS3_Sportback_revealed-28">
        [28]
       </a>
      </sup>
      It went on sale in the first quarter of 2015 and featured a 367 PS 2.5 litre inline five cylinder engine with 465 NM of torque. Production ceased in the second quarter of 2016. The RS 3 Sportback had a seven speed S tronic transmission and quattro all-wheel drive system which helped propel the car to 100 km/h in 4.3 seconds. The RS 3 Sportback out-performs BMW's M2 &amp; Mercedes-Benz's A45 AMG in a straight, thanks to Audi's Quattro feature. Scott Keogh of Audi of America said in April 2015 that he's "confident" we'll see the car come to the United States.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        [51]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In April 2015 the new 2015 RS 3 Sportback was promoted in the UK by a controversial commercial portraying an Audi R8 "giving birth" to it.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        [52]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2017_update">
       2017 update
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: 2017 update">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      After 4 years of its lifetime, the third-generation Audi A3 got a facelift for the model year 2017. The facelifted model was first unveiled through a set of official images in April 2016. The new A3 sedan was given significant cosmetic updates, which were in-line with the automaker's new design philosophy. As a result, the 2017 Audi A3 sedan featured the famous Matrix LED headlamps that were earlier seen in the A8 flagship sedan and the R8 supercar. The front grille was also given a refreshed treatment that made the new A3 look like its elder siblings. Changes on the sides and rear were minimal, with only the taillights getting new LED treatment. There were multiple updates on the interiors as well, with a fully digital 12.3-inch instrument cluster screen placed behind the steering wheel. Currently on sale in Europe and expected to be released in USA and Asia/Pacific 4 QTR 2016
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        [53]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Safety_3">
       Safety
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Safety">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Audi_A3_8V_1.4_TFSI_Ambiente_Misanorot_Interieur.JPG">

        1,968 cc (120 cu in) I4
       </td>
       <td>
        150 PS (110 kW; 148 hp) @ 3,500–4,000
       </td>
       <td>
        320 N·m (236 lb·ft) @ 1,750–3,000
       </td>
       <td>
        8.6 s
       </td>
       <td>
        213 km/h (132 mph)
       </td>
       <td>
        6-speed manual
        <br/>
        6-speed
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct_Shift_Gearbox" title="Direct Shift Gearbox">
         S Tronic
        </a>
        <small>
         (optional)
        </small>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td>
        A3 2.0 TDI
       </td>
       <td>
        1,968 cc (120 cu in) I4
       </td>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_accolades">
       Awards and accolades
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Awards and accolades">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       (2014)
       <a href="/wiki/World_Car_of_the_Year" title="World Car of the Year">
        World Car of the Year
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       (2013)
       <i>
        What Car?
       </i>
       Small Family Car of the Year
      </li>
      <li>
       (2013)
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/What_Car%3F" title="What Car?">
         What Car?
        </a>
       </i>
       Car of the Year
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AV_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AV-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       (2006) South African Car of the Year
      </li>
      <li>
       (2000) Brazilian Car of the Year
      </li>
      <li>
       (1997, 1999, 2000)
       <i>
        Auto Motor und Sport
       </i>
       readers' poll Best Car award
      </li>
      <li>
       (1997)
       <i>
        Autozeitung
       </i>
       "Auto Trophy" award
      </li>
      <li>
       (1996)
       <i>
        Bild am Sonntag
       </i>
       "Golden Steering Wheel" award
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsport">
       Motorsport
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Audi_A3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Motorsport">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Robb_Holland" title="Robb Holland">
       Robb Holland
      </a>
      used an A3 to compete in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014_British_Touring_Car_Championship_season" title="2014 British Touring Car Championship season">
       2014 British Touring Car Championship season
      </a>
      .
     </p>
